Chapter XXXII.
On the treatment of prominent teeth over other teeth.
When the prominent teeth do not follow their natural course and especially when they affect women, and particularly those who are venerable; therefore, you should consider: if a tooth is too close to another tooth and it is impossible to file or apply any substance to it, then you must extract it. But if it is not attached to another tooth, at that time you incise it with this instrument whose shape resembles a pig's tusk, and it is made of Indian iron with an extremely sharp point.
And ensure your incision is such that when you incise it, over the course of several days due to the hardness of the tooth, it does not become connected to other teeth.
And if it is a prominent tooth suitable for filing, then file it with an Indian iron file, which has this shape:
And let it be entirely made of Indian iron and grind it appropriately; it should have small pointed teeth like the file on which needles are made. With this, file the tooth little by little over several days with ease, so that it does not become connected to another tooth and cause harm. And at the end, smooth it with a linen cloth, and polish it with razors.
And if it is a tooth where part of it is broken and you touch the tongue, then you should file down the inside so that the roughness of that fragment is smoothed out and evened, and fill it in so that the tongue does not injure itself nor does speech become impaired.
Chapter XXXIII.
On the restoration of defective teeth with gold or silver filling.
When it happens that the front teeth are damaged by impact or displacement due to an accident or fall, and the patient cannot bite properly as a result, and you have treated them with astringent medicines but your treatment has not been effective, then in order to prevent further damage, you should restore those strong teeth with gold and not silver, because silver can tarnish over time, whereas gold never changes.
And the filling should be in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that can fit between the teeth; the method of the restoration is that you take the filling and place twice its amount between two healthy teeth, and then build up with twists of the filling material between one or more defective teeth until it reaches the adjacent healthy tooth. And then continue the restoration back to the part where you started, and ensure your work is done with ease and skill so that it is not defective.
And when you place the filling, ensure that your handling of the gold or silver does not damage the roots of the teeth.
And then trim the excess filling material with forceps or scissors, and shape it carefully in each place. Convert and conceal these parts between the healthy tooth and the defective one so that they do not injure the tongue. And then file that area as smoothly as a Roman coin.
But if it is loose or broken, repair that or those parts with additional filling material in such a way at all times.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth and of two crooked teeth, as you will see these diagrams:
And when it happens that I return one tooth or two near the placement of each in their places, and they grow back as we have recounted, and they become straight.
And only a good artisan and wise person can do this.
And sometimes a substitute is made from some cause of the bones of a cow, and it is shaped like a tooth, and it is placed in the location where the tooth is missing, and it is fixed as we have said, and remains and serves for that long.
Chapter XXXIV.
On the incision of the bandage which is applied to the tongue and prevents speech.
This ligament which is below the tongue sometimes is natural and one is born with it, or it is accidental and occurs due to an injury that has already healed.
And the operation is to open the mouth of the patient, his head being in this position; and raise his tongue, and then cut that ligament along its length as far as it separates the tongue from its base.
But if there is any hardness or knot in that area, and this is due to the healing of an injury, then you should cut through it along its length until you have severed the ligament and dissolved the knot.
And be careful not to make a cut in the surface of the skin so that you do not sever the arteries and cause a flow of blood.
After washing the residue of the incision with water or vinegar or water and a cloth, place linen below the tongue; this is done so that the bad odor from under the tongue does not spread elsewhere.
If bleeding occurs, place over the area vitriol powder; but if the blood flows, then cauterize the spot with a hot iron, which is suitable for this purpose. And then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Chapter XXXV.
On the extraction of a sublingual cyst.
Sometimes, below the tongue, there appears a swelling resembling a small abscess that prevents the tongue from performing its normal function; and it often enlarges to the point of filling the mouth.
The procedure is to open the mouth wide in front of a light source and examine the swelling.
And if you see it as dark or black in color and hard, to which the swelling does not respond to touch, then do not attempt to treat it forcefully.
And if it is inclined to a whitish color and appears moist, then you should proceed with the operation, cut it with a fine scalpel, and cut it completely; and if blood flows during your procedure, then place over it powdered zinc sulfate, which helps to stop the bleeding.
And then return to your work once you have completed the procedure, washing it with vinegar and salt; and treat it with other remedies as needed until it is healed.
Chapter xxxvi.

When I find in the cheekbone a collection of glands that are somewhat assembled and appear outside, which are called the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the division and they do not heal, then consider whether the abscess is hard, dark in color, and with little sensation; at this point, do not touch it with iron.
And if it is red in color and the root is thick, then do not touch it with iron because of the flow of blood; instead, let it remain inside until it is ripe, and then either you will extract it or it will rupture on its own.
And if it is white in color, soft, and the root is subtle, then that one should be incised.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, whether the abscess has already begun to heal after being treated with rest or if it has diminished in any way; then make the patient sit facing the sun, and place his head to the side, and examine the mouth of the abscess, and the assistant takes between their fingers from below an instrument made of noble material, which has the following form:
And it should be made of silver or iron, and should be as thin as a knife.

But if this instrument is not at hand, then incise with a scalpel which has this form: It is sharp on one side, not sharp on the other side.
And after you have made one incision, make the other according to this method of cutting, and then the wound should be cleansed with water.
But if there is bleeding, cleanse it with water from the decoction of lemon peel or mint leaves and similar substances that are astringent until the flow of blood is stopped, and then proceed to treat it until it is healed.
And sometimes these appear in the groin or as abscesses near those two ears, and incise them according to what I have said about the incision of two cuts similarly.
And I once treated a woman with an abscess that had appeared in her groin, which was dark in color and painful to the touch, causing it to close up the area of the groin, and she breathed through a narrow passage. She had been prohibited from eating or drinking water, and she would have been near death if I had not intervened within one day or two.
And the abscess had become so inflamed that it had formed two channels through which it discharged through two openings.
Then I cut it surgically and placed it in one of their vessels, and pulled that out, and from there the larger portion was removed, and then I incised that where I understood the other part to be joined, and then I closed its mouth, and compressed its tongue, and then I placed the vessel in that abscess.
And then I removed a large part of it, and only a little blood flowed from it. Then the woman was completely cured, and she began to drink water immediately, and soon after she ate food. Therefore, I did not cease to incise that abscess many times over a long period, and another abscess succeeded in its place, which I incised as it became prolonged.
Then I applied something and cauterized the wound of it, then suddenly due to addiction; and after that I wandered around and did not know what God had done for me at that time.
Chapter XXXVII.
On the incision of the breast when it is abscessed.
When one observes catarr in the breast, and it is abscessed and long, it is then called perpendicular; and if it is thick and round in the lower part, it is then called a bubba.
But when it is cured as we have described in the division, and your treatment does not conflict with that cure, and also sometimes there are abscesses that remain stubborn and subtle, then you should incise those that are aggregated and round. And if it extends to a certain length and is bloody, of dark or black color, and is not at the center, then you should attempt its incision because there is fear of malady in that case.
And when you see that according to the method which I have said about its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit and press the tongue with an instrument of which shows its form and immediately place the incision in the new area, and pull it down and incise it with one of two instruments which are mentioned in the incision of two membranes.
And you must not incise it except as much as is naturally appropriate without addition, for if you incise too much, you will impair their speech.
And immediately after the incision, use what we have recommended for the incision of two membranes, and care for it until it is healed.
But if the patient is frightened by the incision, you should use something to cauterize it without causing fear, and the method of cauterization involves only sharp water. Place the head of the patient in your lap, then immediately press the tongue with the instrument which we have described, and subsequently take the water which we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and apply it there as a living cautery, and place it neither thick nor thin, and fill the concavity of the instrument whose shape this is:
Let the extremity of the cautery on which the medicine is placed be like the concavity of a spoon, and place the instrument with the medicine over the ulcer, and the patient should lie on their side so that saliva or mucus from the mouth does not fall on it due to the intrinsic medicine, so that none of this falls onto it and causes harm.
And then take the instrument with the medicine and apply it to the uvula for about a quarter of an hour until you see it become blackened and numbed due to the bite of the medicine.
And if you want, take a piece of cotton and wrap it around the end of the reed, and dip the cotton in the medicine, and insert the reed with the cotton into a tube so that the cotton adheres to that tube, and do this as many times as necessary until you achieve what you want from cauterizing the grape, and then leave it there until it dries and falls off after three or four days.
And if you need to repeat the medicine, do so, and then after cauterizing, clean around the grape with cotton soaked in a bordering solution, and modify what is around it with that which is from the medicine, and wash it with water and soap, and treat it externally with an embrocation, and cure it internally according to the remedies until it is healed.
And this particular method of treatment is safer than incision and longer lasting in terms of avoiding fear.
In some cases, the small grape is cured with something that cauterizes and incises more gently. It is treated by subfumigation in this manner: take wax, hyssop, thyme, rue, Arabian scammony, chamomile, and similar herbs; mix all of these or some of them in a vessel, and soak them in sour wine, then boil it. The mixture should be heated moderately, and at the bottom of the vessel place a tray, on top of which rests an instrument made of wire in this manner; it can be made of silver or wire.
And place the end in the mouth of the vessel so that the vapor reaches the uvula through the tube, until the uvula is sufficiently treated.
Then proceed with those incisions into where it is dry, and be careful not to perform this treatment at the beginning of the onset of abscesses, for it would be too early for the abscess, and it is not appropriate for you to do that, but rather you should wait for the formation and maturation of the abscess.
If this instrument is not present at your disposal, now take a reed and attach to it a piece of horn at one end, so that the mouth of the wound is covered, for the piece of horn prevents the flame from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter XXXVIII.
On the extraction of thorns and of what adheres to the gums and of other causes.
Incisions are made in what adheres to the gum or a fish bone or any other cause.
Then you should extract what is apparent from that, which catches your eye, and after pressing the tongue with an instrument in front of light, so that it becomes clear to you what is in the gum.
And what does not appear and is hidden in the gum, you should make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, for the cause attached to the gum will be easily expelled by vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of bread or lettuce seed or a mouthful of dry bread; or take a piece of dried sea sponge and soak it firmly in vinegar, and then let the patient swallow that, as it reaches the place where thorns are, they will be easily expelled. Take one eel and boil it in honeyed vinegar, then remove its entrails and soak it; or take a rod and soak the medicine on it.
If you do not forget the causes that we have mentioned, now use an instrument of lead in this form:

Chapter XXXIX.
On the Removal of a Leech Attached to the Throat.
When the leech has been treated with what we have said in the division of treatment with medicines and compresses, consider now the throat of the patient in the sunlight, since you have retracted the tongue of the patient with the instrument that we have recommended.
Then if you see the leech, remove it gently with your fingers carefully.
And if it is not possible for you to remove it, now take a concave cannula and insert it into the patient's throat, and then place a heated iron on the concavity of the cannula, and do this several times (until the leech is dead and falls off), and have the patient abstain from water for the entire day.
Take a clean cloth soaked in water and wipe the mouth with it, then rinse the mouth with that water; do not swallow any of it for any reason and let the water remain in the mouth for about an hour one after another as soon as you feel the water cool.
If this is not possible according to what we have recommended, then fumigate the malodor with cyprus or asafoetida by means of the instrument which we have recommended for the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this, and he will recover.
And there is another method of operation in fumigation with that substance, which is to take an earthenware pot containing burning coals and cover it with a cover having a hole in the middle through which you attach the end of the instrument; then proceed with the fumigation from above; have him place his mouth at the end of the tube and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape until you know that the fumigation has reached the bloodsucker, for it will fall immediately upon feeling the smoke.
And if it does not work, then repeat the fumigation as many times as necessary, and prevent the patient from drinking water, and give him salty and dry foods to eat, and let him not drink water. It is also necessary that this regimen be followed strictly.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker is treated when it is seen in the throat; and it resembles forceps as you see them, but there is some curvature to it: which is placed in the throat, and the end of it resembles the beak of a heron, which is sharpened with a file, so that when it grips something, it does not let go.
Chapter XL.
In this chapter is the summary of the discourse on the preparation for the incision and treatment of abscesses.
Abscesses are of various species and in many ways, as will be recalled for each one in this book.
And they differ in the incision and treatment of them by two methods, one of which is according to the nature of the abscess itself; and by what we learn from their humidity.
And the second method is according to the parts of the body where they occur, for an abscess occurring in the head is different from one occurring in the buttocks; and an abscess occurring in fleshy parts is different from one occurring at a joint; and each has its treatment by surgical operation.
And there are some abscesses that should not be incised until they have reached proper maturity or completion.
There are other abscesses that should be treated when they are crosswise and not fully mature according to their completion, such as those near joints, because an abscess near a joint prolongs the substance around it, corrupting the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing contraction of the limb; or if it is near a principal member, delaying its incision until it matures could harm the principal member; or if it is near the buttocks, you should not wait for full maturity before incising it to avoid the pus spreading into deeper parts of the buttocks and forming a fistula, or failing to heal properly. You should know the time for piercing the abscess, and this is when it is ripe.
And you should know that it is ripe when there is relief from the pain and the cessation of fever, and soon after the reduction in heat and pulse, and the sharpness at the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And you should know that the piercing should be done at a place where pus is already present, below the abscess and from where pus will come for the healing of the elevation.
And the piercing should always be done through the thickness of the flesh or body, if the abscesses are in the areas of the limbs or chest, and in places away from the joints, tendons, nerves, arteries; and finally, in any place where there is no reflection; for in those that reflect, use piercing according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy area, the best time is to postpone the piercing until the digestion of the second stage is confirmed, as we have said; for if you pierce it before that, it prolongs the suffering of the patient and causes excessive putrefaction, and makes the lips of the wound hardened and its depth greater.
But some abscesses should be pierced according to the thickness of the flesh or body due to necessity, or according to what that member requires.
And you should administer a small piercing in small abscesses, and in large abscesses, a larger and wider piercing or multiple sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And in other abscesses where it is necessary to incise and open them, when they are made as described, if done at a time when it is already suitable, just like those that occur with excessive boils and buboes.
And of those which are incised with a triangular section; and among these is one that is incised as the figure of a myrtle leaf, just like the abscesses of the angles.
And of those in which a round section and a lunar section are administered, and similar to these.
But in the case where there is none such as their superficial lion abscesses, you should puncture that with a shallow puncture, or just make it flat.
And when the abscess is large and has collected pus, you should puncture it but do not hesitate to extract all the pus at that time; having extracted part of it, on another day scrape the abscess inside, and then extract a larger portion, and continue doing this multiple times according to its severity until it heals.
And especially if the patient is a malnourished adult, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an elderly person in debility, for their vital spirit is quickly resolved with the evacuation of the pus, and the patient may die easily, so you must operate carefully.
Take great care with this chapter and the puncture you perform on these abscesses; clean the plaques and then consider whether the plaque of the abscess is small or if it is a flat section, in which case you should apply some of it or attach it to antiseptic cotton; and if the abscess is large and the cracks of the puncture are many, then you should place wax on each part until they heal.
And if in the abscess a part of the cord is divided or you have concaved it around the circumference, then you should cover it with old cloth or thread made from linen, as when you treat pustules or boils without moisture; and strengthen that on the third day; and thereafter proceed with it and care for it according to what is needed of ointments until it is healed.
If blood flows during the time of your operation, then at that hour administer water mixed with vinegar in which you dip a cloth, and place that over the site of the bleeding for several applications.
If the bleeding continues, then you should administer treatment and cure with powders that I have recommended in various places of this our book and in its division.
If it is in the time of winter, and the site of the abscess is a place with many nerves, then you should apply powders mixed with vinegar and heated oil, and place those on the sites.
And if it is in summer, and the sites are fleshy, then you should apply powders mixed with water and oil or with vinegar and oil, and let all of this be applied for no more than three days, as we have said. Then you should open the abscess, cleanse it, and administer whatever is necessary for its cure until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary to know about the treatment of abscesses generally, but according to the method of distinction I have already described for each type of abscess in a particular manner.
Chapter XLIV.
On the sectioning of abscesses that occur in the neck.
In the neck, small abscesses may occur, along with various types of nodes that contain membranes; and these types vary in many ways.
And they are soft, and those that contain moisture similar to jelly. Of those which contain humidity similar to dust, and resembling them; and of those that are stony, hard.
And in the section of all, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as the extraction of those does not oppose surgery.
And the operation in the section of those is that you should use an instrument whose form approaches this, which is called an entroba, so that you know what it contains.
For if what it contains is humidity, then you should cut that with a section according to its length for a superficial section according to this form:
And begin in the section of the line B to the line G. When the humidity is evacuated, then you should remove that skin which contains that humidity, and do not leave any cause for inflammation, as overly observed return if anything remains from that cause.
And then immerse the piece in Egyptian ointment, if it is available, and if not, in water and salt; and apply that to the wound and leave it for another day, as with this you will dissolve everything that remains of that skin.
And then repeat on that piece with the Egyptian ointment a second and third time if necessary, until you are confident that there is no remaining cause of that skin; now treat the wound with an ointment until it is healed.
And if an abscess contains hard lumps, then you should incise that according to this form: with a section having the shape of a cross, and grasp once between two lips of the section and scrape it thoroughly from all sides, and exert your skill in extracting the membrane that contains it.
If there is opposition from you regarding archery, now do what I have recounted to you first.
And similarly, treat the suppurated boil with respect to its section and cure as we have told you; and the section of a suppurated boil is easier, because it has little blood and little moisture.
And sometimes there are some of these boils that occur on the head in some people who do not have much moisture throughout; the cause is that I once incised a boil on an old woman's head and found it as hard as a stone, rough, white, which could not be scraped off, and if anyone were to strike it, it would hurt them.
But in other boils that occur on the head, this is not the case with this chapter; similarly, for the boils that appear on children's heads and behind their ears, the section of all these should be superficial.
And avoid piercing those in the lower part so that the contents of the boil can drain into the lower parts.
And treat those as is appropriate for their healing.
Chapter XLII.

Chapter XLIII.
On the division of the pustule of an accidental abscess in the groin.
Thus did the ancients call this section in the epitome, and no one has seen such an incision made in our land.

Chapter XLV.
Of the section on the kinds of knots.
There are various kinds of knots, and I have already mentioned all their kinds in the division.
And so I recommend that you distinguish between a knot and an ulcer as this causes doubt.
Therefore, I say that an ulcer is characterized by heat and fever and intense pain inside it, where the bubbling of excess matter subsides; it is completed by putrefaction, which at this point stops the fever, pain, and heat.
But a knot is neither hot nor feverish nor painful, and it resembles the swelling behind the ear which is in its own place.
And it depends on the color of the skin, and its beginning is like a pimple, and it develops in such a way, whether larger or smaller, and there are two kinds of them: dry ones that contain little moisture, and moist ones whose colors indicate humidity, as I describe in the division.

And if there is no moisture from the penetration, then you know that it is greasy.
And if it is dry and has the shape of a cross according to this form: As you have been taught, suspend that part and scrape the wound from all sides with ease, and keep the skin or sack if possible over it and extract that pus at the node.
But if it is torn during the operation, it is not possible to extract that pus, and you should leave it as it is; then you will extract it gradually so that none of it remains for any reason.

And if the node is large, then you should cut both sides of it and treat it with what promotes healing.
But if a pulsating or non-pulsating vein is involved, then you should tie it off and fill the area with vitriol three times so that the wound heals and the boiling of the blood subsides; and after two or three days return to incising what remains of the node.

Chapter XLIX.
On the Incision of Abscesses that Occur Due to Artery or Vein.
When an artery is ruptured and the wound around it has healed, an abscess may occur. The signs by which one can determine whether inflammation and abscess are due to an artery or a vein: when the abscess is due to an artery, it tends to be elongated near the front of the body; and when you press on the abscess with your fingers, you will hear a hissing sound in that area.
And that which is from a vein is round on the surface of the body.
And a section on this abscess is an error, especially in those areas near the armpits, and in the angles, and in the neck, and in many places on the body; for it is dangerous, therefore it should be avoided, and those that are in the extremities or on the head should also be avoided.
For that which is due to inflammation of the artery opening, divide in the long section carefully; and near make the incision with hooks and near the artery, and remove the tunics until it is exposed.
And then place on that needle and make it penetrate into the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread at two places, which I warn you about in the extraction of two arteries, which usually occur in the thighs.
And then press the place which is between two ligaments with a probe until the blood stops there, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer treatment in which pus is generated so that the ligaments fall off; and then treat it with appropriate remedies so that it may be healed.
And if it is an abscess due to the section of a vein, then you should have in your hand what is possible regarding the abscess with caution, and then insert the needle below the place where you had your hand, and make it penetrate; and tie it with double thread so that you can extract it from the other side, and then ligate the abscess with a good ligature as I have told you about in the grapevine ligature on both sides of the thread's ends.
If you fear that you will extract the thread, then insert a needle under the abscess below the point of incision; and place your fingers in four places.
Approach the abscess in its middle part when it is empty of what was inside; then incise the surface of the membrane, and leave what is attached to it.
And then press on the powder which you have mixed with wine and oil, and subsequently administer the treatment made with hot cloths and herbs until it is healed.

Chapter LII.
On the Treatment of Hernias of the Navel.
A hernia of the navel is caused by various reasons; it may be due to fissures in the abdominal wall above the belly, and in such cases, membranes or intestines protrude as they do in other ruptures; or it may be due to a wound from which blood flows from a vein or artery depending on the situation, or it may be caused by trapped air.
But if it is due to a fissure in the abdominal wall and the protrusion of membranes, then the color of the swelling is similar to the color of the body; it does not cause much pain, and can appear in various situations. And if it is by exit from the bowel, then at that moment the situation of that thing which we have recounted differs greatly in degree, and when you press that thing with your fingers, it hides and returns; and quickly it is there, and it is magnified much by the introduction of bath and hard work.
And if due to moisture, then it is soft and does not hide when you press with your hand, nor is it constricted, nor is it hard.
And if it is due to blood, then at that moment these signs appear with the abscess turning to a declining blackness.
And if it is due to flesh lacking moisture, then the abscess is severe, large and hard, and it penetrates in quantity.
And if it is due to gas, then the touch of it is soft.
And the operation in this case is that you consider at this moment whether the prominence of the navel is due to blood from an artery, or from a vein, or due to gas; now it behooves you to be cautious about treating it, for there is fear and dread as I have taught you in the chapter where I have said about abscesses from arteries and veins.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to the bowel or the membrane, then it behooves you to order the patient to have their belly empty and be standing extended; then examine around the entire circumference of the navel with your hand; then order them to stand facing between your hands on their belly; then encircle the area with a strip of linen about an inch wide around the circumference of the navel over the spot you marked with your finger; then extend half of the abscess above toward both sides with a thick bandage or a cloth and tie it securely.
From the side of the swelling of the abscess spread over the bandage and insert your finger into that pus and search for the bag; and if you have found it or secured it by the bandage, now extract it immediately and urge the bag to the parts inside the belly.
And if you have found the cloth, now take it with force; and cut into the excesses of it.
But if it is contrary to your art or vein, now surround that spot, and then return to your operation; and take two needles and place them in those two strong places and insert two needles into the circuit you made around the abscess in a cross manner, which you should make penetrate; and then strengthen the abscess in four parts over the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the area so that the extended flesh can drain and fall off by itself; or incise it when it is thin and let it drain, and then treat it with water as needed until it heals.
And if the swelling of the navel is of flesh or due to moisture, now it is necessary for you to conquer the abscess as we have said and extract the blood or moisture that you find there, and then treat it with water as needed and to consolidate the area.

Chapter LVI.
Of the inflammation that occurs in the foreskin at the head of the penis, and of corruption, blackening, and adherence of the foreskin to the head of the penis.

And then stretch the white duct that is below the groin until it is exposed.
Take the knife and place it above the prominent part of the navel, and press it onto the belly button.
And then apply the two prominent points at the end of the line of the navel, and join them to each other with a suture.
And then extract the end of the knife, and do not incise the navel completely, nor extend the wound, nor for any other reason as I will teach you in the treatment of an intestinal hernia.
And then treat it as you would treat other wounds, and when you incise the area, clean it and restore the wound until it is healed; for the navel is contracted and the prominence of rupture has not been adjusted.
And cautery is better in this location, for it is closer to health.

Chapter lxix.
On Castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, yet for cause it is read to me that I should remember it in this book; and the remembrance of it is not necessary except for two ways, of which one is so that when asked about it, a physician knows how to cure it when it occurs; and the other way is that we have sometimes need to castrate certain animals for our benefit from them, such as horses, oxen, pigs, and similar beasts.
And therefore I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting.
But in the one that is performed by crushing, the method of the operation is that we should immerse the animal in warm water until the testicles become softened and descend. And then take those [testicles] in your hand until they resolve and do not appear below the touch.
But in castration performed by cutting and sectioning, hold the animal and press the scrotum of its testicles with your left hand.
And then lift the scrotum, and make an incision on each side until you proceed with both sides.
And then cut those parts that you will have separated. And do not leave any cause for infection on those parts, but ensure the wound is clean and proper so that it heals over the veins.
And this method of castration is better, which is done by inversion, because inversion leaves some cause of the testicles for the animal to desire sex.
And properly treat the illness until it is healed.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of hermaphrodism.
Hermaphrodozia in men is according to two methods: one is when there appears in the space between the testicles a figure of female parts, where hair also develops.
And sometimes there appears a passage for urine in the space between the testicles.
In women, there is one type: it is that the female organ above the pubis appears as two testicles of a man slightly towards the inside, like the scrotum of a man and two testicles.
And the treatment is of three types: two for men and one for women. And it is that you should cut away those tight tissues until the excess flesh is removed, and then treat them as you would other illnesses.
And in the second type for men, where there is urine passing through a passage between the testicles, there is no treatment or surgery to address it.
Chapter 21.
On the treatment of protrusions and raised flesh due to causes related to women.
The spot is often light in color and is adjusted according to natural causes within which it is situated and is made with regard; and in some women, it is magnified so much that it spreads just as in men and prevails even into intercourse.
Then take the superfluity of linting with your hand or with one piece and incise it.
And do not delay in incising, especially at the beginning of the swelling, so that it does not become a flow of blood.
And immediately treat her with the cure for such wounds so that she may be healed.
Malignant flesh that arises from the ulceration of the mother within which it fills that area and is easily spread to other parts like a tail (and for this reason some of the earliest called it "tail disease"); therefore, we should incise it as we would linting, and treat her so that she may be healed.
Chapter LXXII.
On the Treatment of Ulcers.
Alratica is when the hymen of the woman is not perforated, or the opening is small. And it can be either natural or accidental.
It is accidental due to illness that preceded it, and that is caused either by flesh poorly adjusted or by a subtle or thick obstruction.
And it occurs either at the beginning of the swelling, or on its sides, or in the upper part of it, or in the lower part, and you should prohibit intercourse and pregnancy, and easily prohibit menstruation.
Of that knowledge is made by observation of the menstruation, if the obstruction is apparent, proceed promptly; but if it is not apparent, then wait around there with your fingers or with light.
But if the obstruction is due to a small cicatrix and it has opened between the two lips, then you should cut it and disrupt that.
And it is that you place upon the two lips poultices, and then place your fingers carefully between both of them.
And the woman should lie on her back, her thighs spread apart, and then spread both lips forcefully so that the small cicatrix is ruptured and the obstruction is opened.
And then take linen and dip it in oil and place that on the spot, and let a man hold it there for a day so that the cut area does not heal too quickly.
But if the cicatrix is thick and hard, then it is necessary for you to cut that with a scalpel or with a myrtle leaf.
But if the obstruction is due to flesh, then suspend that for a moment, and incise it.
And prepare the medicines that stop blood flow without causing harm, such as helleborus, dragon's blood, and cerate, mixed with egg white.
And then administer a lead tube that is wide so that the wound does not heal too quickly.
And keep that for several days and administer dry heat.
And this should be treated along with the other treatment for consolidation until it is healed.
And in some cases accidents occur during the major formation of other tissues, and at these times it is necessary to incise according to this method. But if this is due to a chronic abscess, the chronic abscess which is in the main part should not be treated contrary to it in any way.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids and similar conditions that occur in the genital area of women.

Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and tumors when they are in the area of the main part and do not appear to the senses, at this time treatment should not be applied forcefully.
But those that are in the opening of the main part and which can be felt, these are the ones that can be treated.
And it is necessary to place the woman in a warm bath and then extend the tumor with forceps or rough cloth, and incise those that need it with scissors.
And then powder should be applied to those that bleed from one of the powders used for incisions without chewing, such as acacia and similar substances.
Soak the pieces of flesh in cold water for an hour, and then lay it in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then place it in a decoction of sumac, orange peel, walnuts, and similar substances.
And then take flour of barley and mix it with honey and sour wine, and apply a plaster made from this mixture to the back.
And if the blood is clotted, that is good; otherwise, apply two cupping glasses to it, and perform incisions at the sites of the mammary glands.
And then take wool and soak it in the juice of cilantro or aniseed or wild garlic in sour wine, and apply it to the affected area; and afterwards treat the area with ointments until it is healed.
And treat it until it is healed.

Chapter LXXV.
To instruct midwives in how to treat male embryos when there is an unnatural condition as shown in the figure.

Chapter LXXVI.
On the Extraction of a Dead Fetus.
When you are treating a dead fetus as we have said in the division of treatment and it does not come out otherwise, then you must use an operation. At that time, you should consider whether the woman is healthy and free from any of the conditions for which she is feared to suffer loss.
At that time, the woman should be placed on her back on the bed with her buttocks raised and her head lowered.
And the attendant should hold both of her legs or tie her to the bed so that her body does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you should moisten the mother's mouth with olive oil and mastic of hartwort and fenugreek and linseed.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and mastications, and then insert her hand into the mother, and then search with her hand for the place where the hooks are in the fetus.
And the appropriate places for this are as follows: then you should consider whether the fetus is positioned to descend head first, and at that time you place the hooks in its hands, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its chin, or in its clavicle, or in the proper areas of its ribs, or under its armpits.
But if the descent is foot first, then in the navel area, or in the middle of its ribs.
Take the needle in your right hand, and place its curve at that point which is between the fingers of your left hand, and insert it easily into one of those places we have mentioned, until it reaches the diseased area.
And place and insert another needle next to it, or a third if necessary, so that there is equal attraction, and not extension according to its straightness alone.
And do this to all parts, so that the extraction of it is eased in the same way as is done for the painless removal of teeth.
And in the area where extension should be softened; and if any part is resistant, then it is necessary for the midwife to anoint some of those places with oil and insert them carefully and rotate there what is resistant.
Then if the part of the fetus is dislocated, now the needles should be moved to the place that hurts more; and do this until all of the fetus is delivered.
But if the hand is dislocated in front of the other, and it is not possible to reduce it due to its contraction, then wrap a cloth around that one; and subsequently extract that one until all of it is delivered, and cut it either at the joint of the hand or at the elbow.
And do the same for the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or constriction occurs during extraction, or it is in the head of the tightly fitted water bag, then you should insert between the fingers and cut open the head to remove the water, or use an instrument called “alundat,” the shape of which will be among the shapes of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
And it should appear as if the task is of great head by nature: and now it is necessary to incise that tumor which is bound, or to take that tumor out in this way as we have said; and then extract from the bones that which is there with the forceps.
And if the head is swollen and constricted below the clavicle, then it should be split so that the moisture which is in the sinews may effuse.
But if it is not complicated, nor swollen in appearance, then you should incise the head as soon as possible according to what seems best to you.
And if the lower part of the abdomen is abscessed or is in a state of hydrops, then it is necessary for you to puncture that area through which flows the moisture that is there.
But if the tumor is on the upper thighs, then the attraction of it is distant and the direction of it towards the mouth of the urethra is remote.
But if it is constricted below the abdomen and the thighs, then it is necessary for you to extract that tumor wrapped in a cloth which you have enveloped around your hand, and to cut open the abdomen and the thighs so that the fluid that is there may flow out.
But if the other members remain still and turn the head, then place your left hand in between; but if the mouth of the urethra is open, then insert your hand into the prepuce, and search for the head there, and pull it together with those mentioned into the mouth of the urethra, and then insert one or two fingers, and pull them along with that.
And if the mouth of the urethra is constricted by an abscess which has occurred, then it should not be pressed upon; instead, it is necessary to administer moist and fatty applications. Apply plasters; and follow with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the condition is on the side, then at that time, if possible, puncture it; and apply what we have said about the living condition.
And if that is not possible, then cut it into pieces and extract it.
And it is necessary not to leave any cause inside for the second time.
And when you have completed your entire operation, then apply what we have said about the treatment for boils or abscesses that may occur as a result.
And if bleeding occurs, then bathe in astringent waters and proceed with the other treatment.
And I have seen a woman in whose womb there was a dead fetus, and above that focus another pregnancy occurred, and the other fetus was also lifeless. It happened to one who had an abscess near their navel for a long time; it became swollen internally with a fetus, and began to expel water.
And I was called to treat them, and treated them for a long time, but the condition did not improve.
Then I applied to them several causes of strong attraction in the form of plasters, and extracted one bone from them, and after a few days, extracted another bone; and I was very surprised, as there were no bones in the belly.
Then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore, when treating the wound, remove the bones that are present in its various positions, and if it has already been treated for a long time in such a manner, correct it with a small piece of wood.
And it is not strange for this to be so, because in this lies the science and aid for what the surgeon uses his hand to administer in treatment.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary for extracting the fetus.
Form of a spiral in which the largest is used:
This is the form of a clamp with which it equalizes the leaves, to this clamping there are two spirals at the two ends of two branches. However, this spiral should be finer than the string, and it should be made of reed or wood.
And the width of each branch should be about two fingers and the margin of each side about one finger, and the length of each is half a palm plus a little; and in the middle of the two branches there are two adjustments made from the same material as the branches which are fixed, their length being half a palm plus a bit more, and the width of each being about two fingers, or a bit more.
And these two adjustments should be inserted into the mouth of the larger one so that they are opened when you rotate the two prescribed spirals.
Another similar form, but finer and lighter:
It should be made of reed or wood according to the appearance of forceps. However, at the end of the side of the wound make additions in this way as often as necessary, and the length of those additions is about one palm, and the width of each is two of these.
And when you want to open the largest of them, then have the woman lie on her back with her legs hanging down, which is between the thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument in this way as you do with scissors equally according to the quantity that you want from the size of the largest opening until the speculum does what you want.

Of the extraction of the second [incision or procedure].
When the second birth is retained during childbirth, you should command the patient to hold their breath, and then make them sneeze under certain conditions. Place your hand over the mouth and nose of the patient, and if it causes expulsion by this method, that is good.
And if not, then take a vessel and pierce its cover with a hole and place it under the mouth of the mother, along with herbs such as mugwort, chamomile, anise, camomilla, Arabian saffron, cinnamon, and sage. All of these herbs or some of them should be submerged in water in the vessel, and place it over the fire.
And then place a reed tube in the mouth of the mother, and hold it there until the vapor reaches the concavity of the mother.
And then make her sneeze as we have said, and the second birth will be quickly expelled.
But if this treatment delays and is not expelled, then command the midwife to immerse her left hand in sesame oil or malt jelly, and then insert it into the womb and search for the second birth with it. When you find it, pull it out little by little. If it is stuck to the mother's placenta, then insert her hand as we have recommended, and when she finds the second birth, extract it bit by bit so that the mother does not suffer from excessive traction. Take care that it is turned to the right and left with ease.
And if the opening of the mother is narrowed, we have already recommended the treatment through sneezing and the medication of the ulcer with herbs.
But if it is not expelled by all the causes we have recommended, then guard against fatiguing it through repeated attempts at extraction, but rather ensure that what has come out of it and lies in the opening of the mother be attached to the woman's cervix, and subsequently treat it with cauterization; for this will cause it to contract over a few days and it will dissolve and be expelled.
But when you contract it, it causes severe pain in the head and stomach, and this aggravates the illness; therefore, it is necessary to administer sublimations and appropriate treatments for this.
But some of the Ancients already used sublimation of nitrated tartar and dried figs.
Form of the instrument with which a woman is subjected to sublimation due to the retention of menstruation and secondary conditions:
It should be made of wood or horn.
And the thin end should be placed in the vagina and the wide end over the fire, and the sublimation should be placed on the embers of the fire.
And keep that instrument inside until the sublimation is consumed, then repeat with another one.
Of the treatment of the unopened anus of a child.
Many children are born with their anuses not perforated, which must be carefully and skillfully opened. Then it is the midwife's duty to pierce with her finger that said orifice; and if not, she should use a sharp spatula to pierce it, being careful not to touch the rectum.
And then apply poultices made of flour mixed with vinegar and oil; and afterwards, treat that orifice until it is healed.
But if you fear that it is obstructed, then insert a cannula for several days, and remove it when the child wants to pass gas.
And it happens that the anus becomes obstructed due to the consolidation of an abscess or swelling; then it is necessary to incise that consolidation, and afterwards treat it as we have described for treatment with lead.
Of the treatment of fistulas that occur below.
Fistulas that occur in the lower region near the anus are usually small and thick, which often appear near the outside of the anus or in the space between the buttocks.
And it is one fistula or multiple.
And as that small swelling becomes old and discharges watery or pus-like white fluids, and sometimes these fistulas penetrate deeply.
And these deep-seated fistulas are known by what comes out of them through discharge and flatulence; sometimes the discharge is bad, and it easily indicates the nature of these conditions.
Of those fistulas, some extend into the space penetrating into the bladder, and into the shaft of the penis; and some penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the root of the bone.
And in that which is known as a penetrating fistula into the rectum and a non-penetrating one, it is when you insert your finger into the rectum, and introduce a fine thread of hair or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
But if there is tortuosity in that one, then introduce a fine probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or hair with your finger.
And if you do not feel any of that and there is no sign of any cause of evacuation such as pus, worms, or gas, as we have said, then you know it is non-penetrating, and you can proceed with the treatment.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the shaft of the penis, then the significance of that is similar to urine from it and the prohibition is for that which the place requires to be consolidated.
But if it is penetrating into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and there is pain around the area, then the sign of that is that the probe goes through here if there is no tortuosity into the bone, and there is pain around the affected area; and you will have a continuous discharge from it; and medication does not work in that case, nor does it consolidate on its own.
And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is no complete cure, and the treatment for those is the labor and futility of many physicians, upon which such cases depend.
In that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing with iron is expected as I shall tell you, and this is what I and my predecessors have done.
And it is that the patient should lie between your thighs with his buttocks raised and his hips within reach, the objects being inclined towards his belly, and then insert a lead probe or an iron one if it is in the tortuous fistula, until you know where the probe passes.
And if that is the case with the patient around the anus, then you should insert your finger into the anus.
And if you feel with your finger that the probe can easily penetrate, or what you feel between your finger and that tissue or flesh, then you know for certain that it is penetrating; and then do not work on that one, because there is no healing in that one, as we have said.
But some might say that it heals in some men slowly.
And for the treatment in which help is expected, you should ignite a cautery subtly according to the size of the fistula, as was previously described, and insert that heated instrument into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat this two or three times until you know that all those tissues around the fistula are sealed tightly, resembling the quill of a bird.
And then treat that with bandages wrapped in butter until all those sealed tissues heal, and then treat it with medicines that promote flesh growth and consolidation. If it heals, that is good; but if not, then it will not heal at any time by any other treatment.
And if the probe enters and does not penetrate further in, you tell which is inside the anus, and between that and the probe there lies a thin layer of flesh or cicatrix, and sometimes the fistula runs into that part where it lies on the surface of the buttock. Then the region around the beginning of the fistula dries up, and you see that drying extend along with the probe until its tip reaches the place to which the end of the probe extends, and through this the passage is freed and cured.
And then clean those parts of the flesh that are affected by fistulas, which resemble the hollow part of a goose quill and do not tear any part of them for any reason.
But if blood flows out when you are operating on those parts of the flesh, then either the mildest or the pus-filled area should be cauterized with fire or with a sharp medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts two good habits: it tightens the adjusted flesh and stops the bleeding by drying out the moisture.
And then treat that with bandages wrapped in boiled cloth or soft linen until the area gets better, and afterward cure the wound with hard flesh-growing dressings that generate and strengthen new tissue.
And use medicines that have styptic and drying properties; when the area is restored, it is healed and you need not fear recurrence.
But if the fistula already extends inside the base of the anus and is long from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.

Hemorrhoids occur in two ways: either they appear around the anus resembling coal pieces, or they appear like grape clusters. And these can be small or large, and the pus flows continuously from them, and they are single, and appear inside the anus, and at its extremities.

On the treatment of plagues.

Therefore, I say that plagues are varied depending on how the plagues are caused and depending on the location where the plague occurs.

Here are the plagues that are in the parts of the body such as the plague which affects the head, the neck, the feet, the belly, the groin, and similar ones affecting the limbs.

And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite side of the affected part; and keep the patient from overeating and from eating heavy foods.
But if any cause prohibits even this minor intervention, then reduce the patient's food intake and do not allow meat or rich foods.

And if the air has already changed that, then pause for some time until it is healed.

On the treatment of abscesses and fistulas.
Know that every wound and abscess when it becomes old and chronic, and forms an ulcer, and is not consolidated and continues to discharge over time without being excised, whether in any part of the body, is generally called a fistula, and we refer to it as such an abscess.
And truly, a fistula is a soft, hard, white swelling in which there is no pain, but rather itching as with the itching of bird pox; and for this reason it is called a feathered sore, that is, an itch.
And in some people, it is moist, which discharges fluid; and in many cases, this moisture can be excised within a few hours. And at times this moisture is thick, and it is scanty, and it is coarse, and it is fine.
I have shown all those causes, the signs of them, and their cure with medicines in the division.
And it is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of fistulas, which is performed through surgery with my hands.
And you should know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for among them are fistulas that extend to large veins and arteries, or to nerves, or to the brain, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to some of the vertebrae of the back, or to some of the compound joints composed in such a way as those of the hand and foot; and among them are those that reach near the main member and are similar.
And therefore, among these fistulas that follow this manner, they are among the diseases difficult to heal, and do not respond to treatment, and dealing with them requires labor and ignorance.
And if any of the fistulas has a depth that cannot be reached by the places mentioned above and you hope for and trust in its cure and wish to gain knowledge of it, then take a probe of iron or steel, and if the fistula follows a straight path, investigate it with this.
And if the fistula is tortuous, then investigate it with a probe of fine lead, for the lightness of lead's nature causes it to float and bend around the tortuosity.
And if the fistula has openings that are horrifying, it is not within your power to signify upon them with a probe.
Then irrigate the openings through those openings, for the moisture with which you irrigate that one will go to the other openings and flow from them.
And then inquire very carefully according to the method by which you can know whether here there is a bone or nerve, and whether the depth of the fistula is distant or near, or if it is a fistula with multiple openings that lies above all within your strength, within your examination, within which you examine the malady, and the cause of the pain lies beneath your compression upon the place, and similar signs and accidental causes related to an abscess.
And when you have stood upon all those causes with true station, then proceed to the cure according to confidence: and that is that you now consider whether it is a fistula that is apparent nearby or in a salt place, distant from a joint, or of a nerve, or of an artery, or of a vein, or of one of the places which I have told you about.
Now you dry the fistula according to what was said before about its description, and remove what is in that filtration and of corrupted flesh, and what has grown in the opening of the flesh or of similar nature, and treat it until it is healed.
If the fistula is of great depth and runs straight, it is necessary to incise that as far inward as you are able, and then remove all corrupted flesh from it; and then apply bandages wrapped in sharp medicines, and insert them into the cavity of the fistula which you have probed with a probe.

And then treat it with applications that generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
But if it does not heal with that, then you should cauterize it as we have recommended.

Regarding the treatment of the sinuses and the quality of enemas with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged inside, forming a collection of pus, and then it breaks and is perforated, allowing the pus to drain out, leaving the area empty as if it were a vessel, and the skin above it remains thin like cloth, without reaching advanced corruption, and does not affect the bone or nerves or ligaments, it is called a sinus, and is not named fistula.
However, if the space is prolonged within so that corruption takes hold in some member, it is then called a fistula and not a carbuncle.
And the treatment for this is to incise that wound entirely as it revolves, and especially when it has become thin like cloth, and ensure that it does not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
However, if you hope that the wound will adhere and that the corruption has not yet reached its final stage, and there is pus present in the wound, then your treatment should include enemas.
And you must consider the sinus, and if it is large, and the arm that you are treating has a foul odor, then administer an enema with Egyptian medicine consisting of oil, vinegar, and raisins in equal parts, mixed together until the medicine becomes thick like honey.
And then take what is necessary and dissolve it in water and honey; administer the mixture as an enema to the sinus, plug the opening of the wound, and leave the medicine inside for the duration of two hours.
And then remove that medicine after its use; do this for several days until the sinus is cleansed and the odor is eliminated.
And sometimes an enema is given with ash water when you do not have this medicine available; take the ashes of wheat, put them in water; then strain it and administer the enema with it until you are confident that the sinus is cleaned.
And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then administer an enema with honey and water mixed with raisins three times; also give an enema with vinegar and honey mixed, as honey has cleansing properties and vinegar helps the sinus to adhere, especially when the vinegar is rich in astringency and dryness.
And when you have washed certain areas and convince yourself that the sinus is already cleaned out, then wash it with water that helps new flesh to grow.
And it is that you take a decoction of myrtle and dissolve it in rose oil and vinegar; or wash it with certain medicines and other decoctions which have the properties already written about in the chapter on decoctions.
And if the opening of the sinus is narrow and does not admit the nozzle of the syringe, then gradually enlarge it with a small instrument, and place cotton soaked in Egyptian decoction or basilicon decoction inside until it is enlarged.
And similarly, if the opening is too wide, then sew together the edges with stitches and leave them in such a way that they do not interfere with the insertion of the syringe.
And if the opening from which the pus flows is raised to the upper parts, then dry it in the lower part where the pus can flow downward, for when the arm is constricted at the depth of the sinus, flesh will be generated there.
And if it is not possible to dry the sinus near the lower bone as you wish, then make an opening so that the limb can be prepared in such a way that the pus flows freely according to your arrangement and without any hindrance to the arm.
Move the one who is above the opening of the sinus, which you should drain at all times so that what is inside the arm exits. And so that you know whether what flows from the arm is thin or thick, or is undigested or not undigested.
And for this you should consider the location of that sinus, whether the patient feels pain there or not, and whether it is in an abscess.
And as your treatment is prolonged in this manner, and you see that the matter placed over the opening of the sinus has adhered or is about to adhere, then you should loosen it or change it every third day. When you loosen the dressing, then change the cloth for another one and renew the application.
But if from the sinus there is space for subtle pus, then do not despair of its adhesion, because healing will soon follow. For some people in whom flesh generation in their wounds takes a long time, and others in whom the opposite occurs.
And if from the sinus for several days there is undigested matter coming out of the arm, then you know that the sinus will not adhere; and if the adherence of the sinus is delayed and becomes prolonged, then adjust to a drying effect of the medicines. If the medicines are moist in their substance and in their virtue, they should be dried as well when applied, especially when there is an excess of moisture to be removed.
And the most important thing for curing is to take a powder and dissolve it in rose oil, and mix it with another ointment that has been previously prepared in its substance, and apply it to the area as needed.
In that situation, when there is no bandage available, find a piece of cloth and honey; if the honey has been boiled to thicken it, use that. Or take myrrh, aloes, and mastic, grind them all together, sprinkle the powder over honey which is on the fire, and pour this mixture onto a cloth and stretch it over the wound; and pour the thickened honey with the powder into the wound and sprinkle some of it on a cloth and apply that to the wound.
In some cases, administer with the juice of longleaf aristle and root of celestial lily (and it is a celestial lily) and flour of iris and centaury, and use those simple substances or mixtures, grind them together, sieve them, sprinkle the powder over the honey which has been recommended; and use that.
And if the wound has become prolonged and is not healed by this treatment, then you should know that the corruption is in its root, and it affects the bones or other hard parts of the body or the ligaments; now treat it with a fistula cure, as mentioned above.

Of the formation of veins, these are their types.
Veins are of these types, and there are veins wrapped thickly, full of melancholic superfluities that move through the limbs of the body, and their primary occurrence is in the legs, especially in the legs of travelers, workers, and those who carry loads.

And thus when you expose it, from the bandage you should see that white one which is a cord.
And then place the ligature below that white one so that it is elevated and suspended from the bandage, and suspend it with hooks like a lion's claw.

On the treatment of nasal afflictions.
This illness is called "nafir" in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs, and then it changes from one limb to another.
And I have already seen that as I will now tell you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and uncovering her arm, I saw a small inflammation in the funis vein of the arm, and after resting for an hour, I saw that inflammation spreading as if it were wax moving from one place to another, but more quickly than could be expected, like living silver flowing from place to place.
And then the pain moved from that location to the muscle, and it remained there for about an hour.
And with this, it reaches in the other body until it enters the other arm.
And then it retreated to me, spinning throughout the entire body as I saw; and I was greatly amazed by the permutation of its movement and the speed from one member to another. And I had already seen this before in my eyes according to that manner, but I have now seen words which show pain being transferred from one member to another. But I did not see this in my eyes as I did in the woman.
And I did not think this was possible except that the woman was of a different nature, one of dry bodies and exposed veins, and in this way she exhibited the sensation of the air being transferred.
And it is necessary that this does not appear according to this retro-action in those who are delicate and soft, with moist bodies and hidden veins.
And when you want to treat it, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears in the eye as we have said, then you should press firmly on that area and quickly direct your treatment into where that trapped air has come out, and cauterize the spot.
But if you do not see it in your eyes, then you should treat that by inducing the body to expel wind and air, and apply ointments for foul-smelling pills and for senna and similar remedies.
Of the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are varied according to their types, and according to the parts of the body where they strike, as their diversity includes those with large tips, small tips, concave tips, blunt tips, solid ones; and those with three angles, and those that have tongues; and those that are shafts.
Of the signs of the brain when an arrow strikes it and penetrates the bone, and exits at the vertex which is above the brain, there occur severe headaches, scotoma (partial loss of vision), vertigo, stiffness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms, confusion and vomiting of bile, and very quickly speech is cut off and the voice is destroyed. From the wound site comes a white moist substance like flour, and the face appears to have an abundance of moisture.
And so if these signs appear to you, then you must abstain from treatment and the extraction of the arrow unless it is outside.
But the signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart, which is near the left breast, are such that one can tell whether it has penetrated a hard or soft area; and very quickly the movement of the arrow is like the pulse movement, and blood from the wound is black, and coldness seizes the extremities, and cold sweat appears; therefore you will know that death descends soon.
Here are the signs when the arrow has struck the lung: bloody frothy fluid flows from the wound, and the veins near the neck become swollen, and the patient's color changes, and they breathe out great sighs, and seek fresh air eagerly.
And if the arrow hits the membrane in the groin area, and the pain is near the small ribs, and it causes great and violent pain and sighing, and there is no movement at all of the limbs' muscles.
And if the arrow hits the stomach, then immediately after the wound is inflicted, any undigested food causes great pain.
And if the arrow hits the abdomen and is embedded in it, causing some tear of the wound, or the membrane, or intestine which is ruptured, then there is no hope for recovery from the extraction of the arrow.
And if the arrow hits the bladder and urine comes out, and it causes some damage to the parts outside, and immediately there is great pain over the patient, then you know that it is fatal.
But the other limbs as well as the face, the neck, and the jaw, and the shoulders and the arm pits, and the vertebrae of the back, and the clavicle, and the chest and similar parts of the limbs, are saved according to the best practices when the arrow does not hit a vein or artery and is not a venomous arrow.
And I recount this to you as I have seen regarding the nature of these arrows, so that it may be significant for your own treatment.
The cause is that when an arrow struck a man in the lacrimal bone at the root of his nose, I extracted it from the other side, leaving behind only the gray matter of his ear, and he healed without any injury to his eye.
From extracting another arrow from a Jew’s eye, the case being that the arrowhead was embedded in his eyeball, after lifting the eyelid up and down, and the arrowhead was hidden and could not be reached except for a small part to which it adhered with its shaft, and it was a large sharp arrow of those used by the Turks, armed with a lion’s tooth in which there were no barbs.
The senator was the Jew, and no harm came to his eye despite the accident.

Of venesection and of the qualities of using those methods.

Of bloodletting there are two methods: one involves incision and extraction of blood, and the other is bloodletting without incision.
And this bloodletting which is without incision is done in two ways, as it can be with heat or without heat.
And for bloodlettings that are administered with incision and extraction of blood there are fourteen locations on the body, of which one is where phlebotomies are performed in al-nocrati, which is at the very back of the head; another location is just below both sides of the neck; phlebotomies of the chin below the jaw near the mouth; phlebotomies of the two cheekbones; phlebotomies of alohoster, which is above the collarbone; phlebotomies of two armpits; and phlebotomies of two thighs.
And bloodletting that does not extract the blood but rather affects the small veins spread in the flesh, and by this it does not capture the virtue as it would with phlebotomy; nor is it necessary for bloodletting to be done with heat or without heat in any disease caused by repletion, so that the entire body may be evacuated.
But if necessity prompts bloodletting due to illness or continuously, administer it at any time at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, in the middle of the month, and at whatever times may be appropriate.
Therefore, when you encounter any such case among those mentioned, and especially if it is in the third or middle of the month, I command that ventilation be made after two or three hours have passed since midday.
And the benefit of ventilation from the neck is that when it relieves gravity in the head and what has settled in the temples; but it should be done in such a way that it also aids in the evacuation of the entire body.
And this ventilation is at the site of the phlebotomy of the cephalic region.
And it is not advisable to use it on one who has a complete fever, or in one who has a cold, for it can cause great harm to them.
And because of this, it should not be used on the elderly, and those whose heads are often diseased.
But for one who is continuously lying on it, forgetfulness may occur; and because of this, you should command the person performing the ventilation to pause their work briefly by lifting the cup away from the area to prevent the generation of forgetfulness.
But ventilation of the forehead is at the site of phlebotomy of the dark vein and the basilic vein: and because of this, it relieves asthma, constriction of the chest, splitting of the sternum, coughing, and congestion.
And it is necessary to apply the forehead cupping lightly, for if it is left too long, it can cause weakness in the body and in the stomach.
And the ventilation of the temples relieves pain in the head, ophthalmia, headache, nasal congestion, and pain in the roots of the teeth; and it is at the site of phlebotomy of the basilic vein.
And you should order the barber-surgeon not to press too hard with his hand during incision so as not to cut an artery and cause a flow of blood.

And order the barber-surgeon not to proceed too much in incision, for the area is bare of flesh, and leave it lest you injure nerves and arteries.

Thus begins the chapter of the third part: on restoration. This chapter is often considered necessary in the art of medicine; it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations of bones.
Oh, son, be aware that those who boast about this chapter are foolish doctors and the vulgar, as well as those who for any length of time have not regarded the books of the Ancients or read a single letter from them.
And for this reason it is done that this method of the scientists in our land is private; and I have not forgotten it for any length of time at all; and I have not applied what follows, but through the length of reading the books of the Ancients and studying to understand them, until I extracted the science from them.
And then I directed myself to experimentation and study throughout the length of my life.
And I have already described in this chapter all that my science contains and on which my experience is based; now I abbreviate it for you and free it from the burden of lengthiness; and abbreviate it to the point of brevity; and demonstrate it at the end of clarification; and form many forms of the instruments used therein, as added by explanation, just as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
First chapter.
A summary and collection of fractures of the bones, from which a preliminary explanation is necessary before we begin to recall the parts of fractures and their various types. Therefore, let us proceed with the prologue of this chapter to summarize the discourse; and the chapters that are essential for understanding at the beginning are necessary for the craftsman and to stand on the truth of those things; it is for you and others like you who wish to know or learn this noble art.
And so I say that when it happens to someone to have a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or fall, at that moment it is necessary for you to consider at the beginning whether to perform venesection or to bandage them, or any other immediate treatment, if there are no prohibitive causes, such as weakness of strength, or if it happens to an infant, or an elderly person in decline, or during a time of extreme heat or severe cold.
And you should be content with food such as fresh herbs and the meat of birds and small animals; we prohibit fatty meats and foods that fill the body excessively, and all food that fills the veins with blood, until you are sure of an abscess being cured, and if you do not fear an effusion of matter into the limb.
And now return the patient to their original regimen that they were accustomed to follow.
And so when the broken bone begins to be restored, it is necessary that the patient be fed with nutritious foods that are moist and heavy, in which there is viscosity, such as food made from boiled wheat with water, rice, peas, beef tripe, eggs, fresh fish, and similar foods, and with this regimen, healing of the fracture occurs more easily and better.
